                        cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical assembly and superior sodium storage properties of a sea-sponge structured C/SnS@C nanocomposite</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Shipei; Xing, Ke; Wen, Jiahao; Wen, Ming; Wu, Qingsheng; Cui, Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">17</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7631-7638</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The exploration of electrode materials with superior rate capability and cyclability has been a crit. challenge for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Herein, a new sea-sponge structured C/SnS@C nanocomposite has been fabricated through the hierarchical assembly of SnS2 nanoflakes on sea-sponge-like macrochannel-interconnected carbon spheres (S-MCSs) and subsequent carbon coating together with the phase transformation of SnS.  A notably enhanced performance is achieved which is attributed to the formation of the sea-sponge-like rigid structure and layered SnS nanoflakes, which facilitate Na+ diffusion at a large c.d. based on the conductive S-MCS skeleton and carbon coating, thus significantly improving the kinetic process of Na+ insertion/extn.  When applied as an anode material for SIBs, the designed C/SnS@C composite exhibits superior cycling stability.  It can endure a c.d. of 10 A/g to complete the charge process in 22 s and deliver a capacity of 370 mA h/g at 1 A/g after five initial activation processes, with over 84% capacity retention from the 200th to the 2000th cycle, which is equiv. to 0.009% decay per cycle.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpoZ0u4eFk2e7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljWn0CG3T8quQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXnsFSks7k%253D&amp;md5=d13abd05caf659804cabb3898d017e85</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.0c11756"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sari, H.                         cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Large Interlayer Spacing of Few-Layered Cobalt-Tin-Based Sulfide Providing Superior Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dou, Shuming; Xu, Jie; Sari, Hirbod Maleki Kheimeh; Wu, Hong-Hui; Hu, Junhua; Zhang, Yaohui; Fan, Linlin; Xiong, Dongbin; Zhou, Wei; Chen, Yanan; Li, Xifei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">37</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">41546-41556</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Mixed transition metal sulfides (MTMSs) have been regarded as a potential anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to their high reversible specific capacity.  Herein, nanoflower-like few-layered cobalt-tin-based sulfide (F-CoSnS) with a large interlayer spacing is synthesized via a facile route for superior sodium storage.  The growth mechanism of this unique F-CoSnS is systematically studied.  Such distinctive nanostructured engineering synergistically combines a broad interlayer spacing (~ 0.85 nm), the functionalities of few (2-3) layers, and the introduction of heterogeneous metal atoms, reducing the ion diffusion energy barrier for high-efficiency intercalation/deintercalation of Na+ ions, as revealed by d. functional theory (DFT) calcns.  With further incorporation of a three-dimensional (3D) conductive network, the F-CoSnS@C electrode shows a large sodium storage capacity (493.4 mAh g-1 at 50 mA g-1), remarkable rate capability (316.1 mAh g-1 at 1600 mA g-1), and superior cycling stability (450 mAh g-1 at 50 mA g-1 with 91.2% capacity retention, 0.044% fading rate per cycle, and approx. 100% Coulombic efficiency after 200 cycles).  This work demonstrates that the few-layered ternary MTMSs are highly applicable for the development of advanced SIB anode materials with high performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoE87sJrTM6arVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljWn0CG3T8quQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhs1ShtrnN&amp;md5=2c0a7a83661bbd65df51ba218d00d60a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.0c00020"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ou, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, W.-B.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Bimetallic Sulfide Sb<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>@ FeS<sub>2</sub> Hollow Nanorods as High-Performance Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Nano</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>14</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">3</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">3610</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">3620</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Bimetallic Sulfide Sb2S3@FeS2 Hollow Nanorods as High-Performance Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cao, Liang; Gao, Xuanwen; Zhang, Bao; Ou, Xing; Zhang, Jiafeng; Luo, Wen-Bin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3610-3620</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Constructing a heterojunction and introducing an interfacial interaction by designing ideal structures have the inherent advantages of optimizing electronic structures and macroscopic mech. properties.  An exquisite hierarchical heterogeneous structure of bimetal sulfide Sb2S3@FeS2 hollow nanorods embedded into a nitrogen-doped carbon matrix is fabricated by a concise two-step solvothermal method.  The FeS2 interlayer expands in situ grow on the interface of hollow Sb2S3 nanorods within the nitrogen-doped graphene matrix, forming a delicate heterostructure.  Such a well-designed architecture affords rapid Na+ diffusion and improves charge transfer at the heterointerfaces.  Meanwhile, the strongly synergistic coupling interaction among the interior Sb2S3, interlayer FeS2, and external nitrogen-doped carbon matrix creates a stable nanostructure, which extremely accelerates the electronic/ion transport and effectively alleviates the vol. expansion upon long cyclic performance.  As a result, the composite, as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries, exhibits a superior rate capability of 537.9 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1 and excellent cyclic stability with 85.7% capacity retention after 1000 cycles at 5 A g-1.  Based on the DFT calcn., the existing constructing heterojunction in this composite can not only optimize the electronic structure to enhance the cond. but also favor the Na2S adsorption energy to accelerate the reaction kinetics.  The outstanding electrochem. performance sheds light on the strategy by the rational design of hierarchical heterogeneous nanostructures for energy storage applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrwpBkuzvl5DbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljw_0m2SPCF_g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXktlOgsLc%253D&amp;md5=781fe918309ad3fe806dcdcc1b39041f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201601329"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, S. Na storage, offering possibilities to develop new anode materials for Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGro-iCD2saXDrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhe8KFibWY5pw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXmtlekurw%253D&amp;md5=e53417f90a62bfd1ec54a5eeba13b17d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit23" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.8b00931"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Long, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Solid-Solution Anion-Enhanced Electrochemical Performances of Metal Sulfides/Selenides for Sodium-Ion Capacitors: The Case of FeS<sub>2–x</sub>Se<sub>x</sub></span>. <i>ACS Appl.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Solid-Solution Anion-Enhanced Electrochemical Performances of Metal Sulfides/Selenides for Sodium-Ion Capacitors: The Case of FeS2-xSex</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Long, Yaqiong; Yang, Jing; Gao, Xin; Xu, Xuena; Fan, Weiliu; Yang, Jian; Hou, Shifeng; Qian, Yitai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition-metal sulfides/selenides are explored as advanced electrode materials for nonaq. Na-ion capacitors, using FeS2-xSex as an example.  A solid soln. of S/Se in FeS2-xSex allows it to combine the high capacity of FeS2 and the good diffusion kinetics of FeSe2 together, thereby exhibiting excellent cycle stability (∼220 mAh/g after 6000 cycles at 2 A/g) and superior rate capability (∼210 mAh/g at 40 A/g) within 0.8-3.0 V.  These results are much better than those of FeS2 and FeSe2, confirming the advantages of S/Se solid soln., as supported by EIS spectra, DFT calcns., and electronic cond.  As FeS2-xSex is paired with the activated C (AC) as Na-ion capacitors, this device is also better than Na-ion batteries of FeS2-xSex//Na3V2(PO4)3 and Na-ion capacitors of metal oxides//AC, particularly at high rates.  These results open a new door for the applications of sulfides/selenides in another device of electrochem. energy storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqAHJGlTpqQo7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhe8KFibWY5pw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXks1ygsbY%253D&amp;md5=a5ff03ce47438934f99747947332aa1a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202010041"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ran, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Design Strategies of 3D Carbon-Based Electrodes for Charge/Ion Transport in Lithium Ion Battery and Sodium Ion Battery</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Design Strategies of 3D Carbon-Based Electrodes for Charge/Ion Transport in Lithium Ion Battery and Sodium Ion Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Tianyun; Ran, Fen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Advanced 3D carbon-based electrodes have the potential to significantly enhance the energy-power d. of lithium ion batteries and sodium ion batteries, due to their continuous conductive networks, proper porosity distribution, and integrated stable structure.  However, it still remains a fundamental scientific challenge to accurately understand the charge/ion transport in 3D carbon-based electrodes.  In this , the operating mechanism of charge/ion transport in 3D carbon-based electrodes are comprehended by introducing a useful architectural analogy to provide a phys. insight.  In order to better understand the relationship between 3D carbon-based electrode structure and electrode process characteristics, the main design strategies of 3D carbonbased electrodes according to the specific characteristic of pore tortuosity is proposed.  Through anal. of 3D carbon electrode architectural models, several key scientific issues and related characterization technologies that are beneficial to improving the charge/ion transport efficiency are also raised.  The kinetics difference of ionic transport between Li+ and Na+ ions is also taken into account.  Furthermore, the crit. parameters of porous structure including porosity and tortuosity to investigate the parameter-structure-performance relationships of 3D carbon-based architecture electrodes are highlighted, which in turn would guide more rational battery design in tradeoff between the high capacity and fast transport.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq1lSYU-3y7I7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhe8KFibWY5pw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Vanadium Sulfide on Reduced Graphene Oxide Layer as a Promising Anode for Sodium Ion Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Ruimin; Wei, Qiulong; Li, Qidong; Luo, Wen; An, Qinyou; Sheng, Jinzhi; Wang, Di; Chen, Wei; Mai, Liqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">As an alternative system of rechargeable Li-ion batteries, Na-ion batteries revitalize researchers' interest due to the low cost, abundant Na resources, and similar storage mechanism to Li ion batteries.  VS4 has emerged as a promising anode material for SIBs due to low cost and its unique linear chains structure that can offer potential sites for Na storage.  Herein, the authors present the growth of VS4 on reduced graphene oxide (rGO) as SIBs anode for the 1st time.  The VS4/rGO anode exhibits promising performance in SIBs.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The exploration of ideal electrode materials overcoming the crit. problems of large electrode vol. changes and sluggish redox kinetics induced by large ionic radius of Na+/K+ ions is highly desirable for sodium/potassium-ion batteries (SIBs/PIBs) toward large-scale applications.  The present work demonstrates that single-phase ternary cobalt phosphoselenide (CoPSe) in the form of nanoparticles embedded in a layered metal-org. framework (MOF)-derived N-doped carbon matrix (CoPSe/NC) represents an ultrastable and high-rate anode material for SIBs/PIBs.  The CoPSe/NC is fabricated by using the MOF as both a template and precursor, coupled with in situ synchronous phosphorization/selenization reactions.  The CoPSe anode holds a set of intrinsic merits such as lower mech. stress, enhanced reaction kinetics, as well as higher theor. capacity and lower discharge voltage relative to its counterpart of CoSe2, and suppressed shuttle effect with higher intrinsic elec. cond. relative to CoPS.  The involved mechanisms are evidenced by substantial characterizations and d. functional theory (DFT) calcns.  Consequently, the CoPSe/NC anode shows an outstanding long-cycle stability and rate performance for SIBs and PIBs.  Moreover, the CoPSe/NC-based Na-ion full cell can achieve a higher energy d. of 274 Wh kg-1, surpassing that based on CoSe2/NC and most state-of-the-art Na-ion full cells based on P-, Se-, or S-contg. binary/ternary anodes to date.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrGdeOmnJzeJbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhe8KFibWY5pw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXmtFajt70%253D&amp;md5=4ac79e28321803529457a2016ae22dd4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1039/C6CP00651E"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jache, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Binder, J.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The abundance of sodium has recently sparked considerable interest in sodium-ion batteries (NIBs).  Their similarity to conventional lithium-ion technol. is obvious; however, the cell chem. often significantly deviates.  Graphite, although being the std. neg. electrode in Li-ion batteries, is largely inactive for Na-ion storage in conventional non-aq. carbonate-based electrolytes, for example.  Very recently, it has been demonstrated that graphite can be activated for Na-ion storage in cells with ether-based electrolytes.  The storage mechanism is based on co-intercalation of solvent mols. along with the Na-ions, forming ternary graphite intercalation compds. (t-GICs).  This process is highly reversible but yet poorly understood.  Here, a comprehensive study is provided on the formation and the stability of t-GICs.  A series of ether solvents are being discussed: linear glymes with different chain lengths (mono-, di-, tri-, and tetraglyme), several derivs. with side groups as well as THF as a cyclic ether and one crown ether.  It is shown that the redox potentials shift depending on the ether chain length and mixing of ethers might enable tailoring of the redox behavior.  The inferior behavior of triglyme is likely due to the less ideal ion coordination.  Complementary expts. with lithium are made and demonstrate the superior behavior of sodium.  It was found that the increase in graphene layer spacing during intercalation only slightly depends on the chain length and is in the range of 250%, and still mech. stability is preserved.  It is further shown that the t-GICs possess chem. stability and demonstrated that the kinetically favored charge transfer is probably due to the absence of a solid electrolyte interphase.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGroQkB8YjSNVbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhg8v5FNSIByg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xlt1Oqsr0%253D&amp;md5=5d74083ea3e2c5f3295d3c0a5b355b85</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1039/C8TA05612A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qin, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Z.-S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">2D Holey Cobalt Sulfide Nanosheets Derived from Metal–Organic Frameworks for High-Rate Sodium Ion Batteries with Superior Cyclability</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">2D holey cobalt sulfide nanosheets derived from metal-organic frameworks for high-rate sodium ion batteries with superior cyclability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dong, Yanfeng; Shi, Wen; Lu, Pengfei; Qin, Jieqiong; Zheng, Shuanghao; Zhang, Bingsen; Bao, Xinhe; Wu, Zhong-Shuai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">29</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">14324-14329</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium ion batteries (SIBs) for large-scale grid applications are facing great challenges in terms of development of high-performance electrode materials and screening of suitable electrolytes.  Herein, a versatile and scalable protocol for synthesizing two-dimensional (2D) holey cobalt sulfide (h-Co4S3) nanosheets is demonstrated for high-rate and long-life SIBs in an ether-based electrolyte of 1.0 M NaCF3SO3 in diglyme.  The 2D h-Co4S3 nanosheets are prepd. by sulfuration of leaf-like cobalt based metal-org. frameworks (CoMOFs), and subsequent annealing treatment.  Benefiting from the nanosheet nature of in-plane nanopores (10-30 nm), ultra-thinness (&lt;30 nm), crumpled morphol., and micron-scale lateral size that can provide more active sites and enhanced sodiation/desodiation kinetics, the resulting h-Co4S3 nanosheets achieve a high reversible capacity of 571 mA h g-1 at 0.1 A g-1, and long-life cycling stability with a retention of 80% after 400 cycles for SIBs.  Furthermore, theor. simulation reveals the enhanced structural stability of h-Co4S3 nanosheets with a lower binding energy (0.31 eV) of the Co-O bond in the ether-based electrolyte than that in the carbonate-based electrolyte.  Notably, the h-Co4S3 anode offers an exceptional rate capacity of 257 mA h g-1 at 12 A g-1, outperforming most reported cobalt sulfide-based anodes.  This strategy will pave a new way to rationally construct MOF-derived 2D nanostructures for various energy-related applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrjoyTnaqZG0LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhg8v5FNSIByg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXht1CisL7M&amp;md5=b071d59cf68f278be92cab3b7de877f8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2020.137379"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tian, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sandwich-Structured Dual Carbon Modified Bismuth Nanosphere Composites as Long-Cycle and High-Rate Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Electrochim.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sandwich-structured dual carbon modified bismuth nanosphere composites as long-cycle and high-rate anode materials for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hu, Chenjing; Zhu, Yansong; Ma, Guangyao; Tian, Fang; Zhou, Yanli; Yang, Jian; Qian, Yitai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">365</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Bi as alloy-based anode material has a high theor. specific capacity (385 mAh g - 1) and volumetric capacity (3800 mAh cm-3).  However, its severe vol. expansion during the alloying process will cause structural collapse and capacity degrdn.  Dual C materials contg. outmost thin C layer and graphene are employed to modify Bi nanospheres to form a sandwich-like C/Bi/reduced graphene oxide composite (CPVP+C2H2/Bi/rGO), which is fabricated via a facile solvothermal method and subsequent CVD strategy.  The thin C layer coated on the surface of Bi nanoparticles can effectively suppress the huge vol. changes of Bi.  The graphene oxide as a conductive matrix favors the successful loading of Bi nanospheres, which limits the particle aggregation of Bi upon cycling.  The dual C also can improve the cond. of the overall electrode.  As anode materials for Na-ion batteries, the CPVP+C2H2/Bi/rGO shows excellent Na storage performance, better than CPVP/Bi/rGO.  At a high c.d. of 5 A g - 1, this electrode can retain a capacity of up to 327.6 mAh g - 1 after 1200 cycles.  The assembled full battery with CPVP+C2H2/Bi/rGO as anode and Na3V2(PO4)3/rGO as cathode also presents good electrochem. performance.  The outstanding electrochem. performance of CPVP+C2H2/Bi/rGO is attributed to the well-designed sandwich-like composite structure and synergistic effect of dual C and Bi nanospheres.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGocA8qVG4IWKLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhg8v5FNSIByg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXit1OiurzL&amp;md5=3c76c8e8dac55102687ebf544a5f3a4c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2016.01.040"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, D.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, B.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.-P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, R.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.-L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Dual-Carbon Enhanced Silicon-Based Composite as Superior Anode Material for Lithium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Dual-carbon enhanced silicon-based composite as superior anode material for lithium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Jie; Liu, Dai-Huo; Wang, Ying-Ying; Hou, Bao-Hua; Zhang, Jing-Ping; Wang, Rong-Shun; Wu, Xing-Long</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Dual-carbon enhanced Si-based composite (Si/C/G) has been prepd. via employing the widely distributed, low-cost and environmentally friendly Diatomite mineral as silicon raw material.  The prepn. processes are very simple, non-toxic and easy to scale up.  Electrochem. tests as anode material for lithium ion batteries (LIBs) demonstrate that this Si/C/G composite exhibits much improved Li-storage properties in terms of superior high-rate capabilities and excellent cycle stability compared to the pristine Si material as well as both single-carbon modified composites.  Specifically for the Si/C/G composite, it can still deliver a high specific capacity of about 470 mA h g-1 at an ultrahigh c.d. of 5 A g-1, and exhibit a high capacity of 938 mA h g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 with excellent capacity retention in the following 300 cycles.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Facile synthesis and electrochemical sodium storage of CoS2 micro/nano-structures</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Xue; Zhang, Kai; Lei, Kaixiang; Li, Fujun; Tao, Zhanliang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">We report the synthesis and electrochem. sodium storage of cobalt disulfide (CoS2) with various micro/nano-structures.  CoS2 with microscale sizes are either assembled by nanoparticles (P-CoS2) via a facile solvothermal route or nanooctahedrons constructed solid (O-CoS2) and hollow microstructures (H-CoS2) fabricated by hydrothermal methods.  Among three morphologies, H-CoS2 exhibits the largest discharge capacities and best rate performance as anode of sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Furthermore, H-CoS2 delivers a capacity of 690 mA·h·g-1 at 1 A·g-1 after 100 cycles in a potential range of 0.1-3.0 V, and ∼240 mA·h·g-1 over 800 cycles in the potential window of 1.0-3.0 V.  This cycling difference mainly lies in the two discharge plateaus obsd. in 0.1-3.0 V and one discharge plateau in 1.0-3.0 V.  To interpret the reactions, X-ray diffraction (XRD) and transmission electron microscopy (TEM) are applied.  The results show that at the first plateau around 1.4 V, the insertion reaction (CoS2 + xNa+ + xe- → NaxCoS2) occurs; while at the second plateau around 0.6 V, the conversion reaction (NaxCoS2 + (4 - x) Na+ + (4 - x)e- → Co + 2Na2S) takes place.  This provides insights for electrochem. sodium storage of CoS2 as the anode of SIBs.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Metal-org. frameworks (MOFs) have been intensively used as the templates/precursors to synthesize complex hollow structures for various energy-related applications.  Herein a facile two-step diffusion-controlled strategy is reported to generate novel MOFs derived hierarchical hollow prisms composed of Nanosized CoS2 bubble-like subunits.  Uniform zeolitic imidazolate framework-67 (ZIF-67) hollow prisms assembled by interconnected nanopolyhedra are first synthesized via a transformation process.  Afterwards, these ZIF-67 building blocks are converted into CoS2 bubble-like hollow particles to form the complex hollow prisms through a sulfidation reaction with an addnl. annealing treatment.                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Fabrication of an MOF-derived heteroatom-doped Co/CoO/carbon hybrid with superior sodium storage performance for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kaneti, Yusuf Valentino; Zhang, Jun; He, Yan-Bing; Wang, Zhijie; Tanaka, Shunsuke; Hossain, Md.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Metal-org. frameworks (MOFs) have gained significant attention as precursors for the fabrication of porous hybrid materials due to their highly controllable compn., structure and pore size.  However, at present, MOF-derived materials have rarely been studied as anode materials for Na-ion batteries.  The authors report the fabrication of a Ni-doped Co/CoO/N-doped C (NC) hybrid using bimetallic Ni-Co-ZIF as the starting precursor.  The resulting Ni-doped Co/CoO/NC hybrid is highly microporous with a high sp. surface area of 552 m2 g-1.  When employed as an anode material for Na-ion batteries, the Ni-doped Co/CoO/NC hybrid exhibited both good rate performance with a high discharge capacity of 218 mA h g-1 at a high c.d. of 500 mA g-1 and good cycling stability, as a high discharge capacity of 218.7 mA h g-1 can be retained after 100 cycles at 500 mA g-1, corresponding to a high capacity retention of 87.5%.  The excellent electrochem. performance of the Ni-doped Co/CoO/NC hybrid for SIBs may be attributed to the synergistic effects of various factors, including: (a) the presence of a C matrix which provides protection against aggregation and pulverization during sodiation/desodiation; (b) the highly microporous nature along with the presence of a few mesopores which facilitates better insertion/de-insertion of Na+ ions; (c) the Ni-doping which introduces defect sites into the at. structure of CoO via partial substitution, thus enhancing the cond. of the Co oxide (CoO) component and hence, the overall hybrid material, and (d) the N-doping which promotes a faster migration speed of Na ions (Na+) across the C layer by creating defect sites, thereby improving the cond. of the C frameworks in the hybrid material.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqWR9Qrpy6E07Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhxq92gLfWNeA"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">In recent years, graphene has been considered as a potential "miracle material" that will revolutionize the Li-ion battery (LIB) field and bring a huge improvement in the performance of LIBs.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The further development of flexible electronics inevitably requires conductive materials to have numerous foldable properties; however, that has not been realized.  Here, inspired by silkworm cocooning processes, we prep. a super-foldable conductive carbon material with layered nanofiber network structures through an improved electrospinning/carbonization technique.  It can remarkably bear 1,000,000 times repeated true-folding without structural damage and cond. fluctuations.  The root of such performance breakthrough is revealed through real-time SEM folding observation and mech. simulations.  Its structures featuring appropriate pores, non-crosslinked junctions, slidable nanofibers, separable layers, and a compressible network can act synergistically to generate a ε-like folding construction at crease under true-folding, which can completely disperse stress via bulged layers, dispersed arcs, and slidable grooves in ε.  Consequently, each nanofiber avoids directly facing with 180° folding when the whole material is true-folded.  This work embodies structure innovation, performance breakthrough, and mechanism reveal, which has great scientific significance and application prospects.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrubhisTXYUR7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhxq92gLfWNeA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XitFajtL8%253D&amp;md5=65dbfa9bfa000fcc523311c904202866</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1016/j.scib.2019.06.014"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wen, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hollow Nanostructure of Sea-Sponge-C/SiC@ SiC/C for Stable Li<sup>+</sup>-Storage Capability</span>. <i>Sci.         </div><div class="casAbstract">An improved method for the prepn. of graphene oxide (GO) is described.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Recent progress in flexible electronics has attracted tremendous attention.  However, it is still difficult to prep. superfoldable conductive materials with good biocompatibility, high sensing sensitivities, and large sp. surface areas.  It is expected that biomimetic methods and water-sol. precursors like poly(vinyl alc.) (PVA) for electrospinning will be utilized to solve the above problems.  Inspired by the multistage water management process of a spider spinning dragline silk, we have established a combined biomimetic technique, hydrocolloid electrospinning coupled with temp. gradient dehydration, with a carbonization technique.  PVA-driven superfoldable carbon nanofiber membranes (PVA-SFCNFMs) have been prepd. that not only possess a &gt;60% micropore ratio and a 1368.8 m2/g sp. surface area but also can withstand 180° real folding for 100 000 cycles, approaching the thickness limit without structure fracture.  Furthermore, these membranes provide highly sensitive sensing and superior biocompatible interfaces.  The mol. mechanism to improve carbon conversion and the folding mechanism to obtain "three-level dispersing stress" for the PVA-SFCNFMs have been proposed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoFMzosnQ_oELVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljUDtmB7sZ6Fg"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Bioinspired Nanocomposites with Self-Adaptive Stress Dispersion for Super-Foldable Electrodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zan, Guangtao; Wu, Tong; Zhang, Zhenlei; Li, Jing; Zhou, Junchen; Zhu, Feng; Chen, Hanxing; Wen, Ming; Yang, Xiuchun; Peng, Xiaojun; Chen, Jun; Wu, Qingsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Science (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2103714</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In flexible electronics, appropriate inlaid structures for stress dispersion to avoid excessive deformation that can break chem. bonds are lacking, which greatly hinders the fabrication of super-foldable composite materials capable of sustaining numerous times of true-folding.  Here, mimicking the microstructures of both cuit cocoon possessing super-flexible property and Mimosa leaf featuring reversible scatheless folding, super-foldable C-web/FeOOH-nanocone (SFCFe) conductive nanocomposites are prepd., which display cone-arrays on fiber structures similar to Mimosa leaf, as well as non-crosslinked junctions, slidable nanofibers, separable layers, and compressible network like cuit cocoon.  Remarkably, the SFCFe can undergo over 100 000 times of repeated true-folding without structural damage or elec. cond. degrdn.  The mechanism underlying this super-foldable performance is further investigated by real-time SEM folding characterization and finite-element simulations.  The results indicate its self-adaptive stress-dispersion mechanism originating from multilevel biomimetic structures.  Notably, the SFCFe demonstrates its prospect as a super-foldable anode electrode for aq. batteries, which shows not only high capacities and satisfactory cycling stability, but also completely coincident cyclic voltammetry and galvanostatic charge-discharge curves throughout the 100 000 times of true-folding.  This work reports a mech. design considering the self-adaptive stress dispersion mechanism, which can realize a scatheless super-foldable electrode for soft-matter electronics.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrdBkT4XbrkyrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg7jGE00HlKAw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XmsFSns7k%253D&amp;md5=9b61ac21bf8cd6d4b2189bb893841be4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201912924"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luan, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lou, X.                         cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrospun Sb/C Fibers for a Stable and Fast Sodium-Ion Battery Anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Yujie; Han, Xiaogang; Xu, Yunhua; Liu, Yihang; Zheng, Shiyou; Xu, Kang; Hu, Liangbing; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered a top alternative to Li-ion batteries (LIBs) for large-scale renewable energy storage units due to their low cost and the abundance of Na-bearing precursors in the earth's mineral deposits.  However, the development of anode materials for SIBs to date was mainly limited to carbonaceous materials with minimal research devoted to high capacity alloy-based materials.  An Sb/C electrode with ∼30 nm Sb nanoparticles (NPs) uniformly encapsulated in interconnecting 1-dimensional (1D) 400 nm C fibers (denoted as SbNP@C) was fabricated using a simple and scalable electrospinning method.  This binder-free, current collector-free SbNP@C electrode demonstrated high capacity and stable long-term cycling performance at various current densities.  The SbNP@C electrode showed an initial total capacity of 422 mA-h/gelectrode and retained 350 mA-h/gelectrode after 300 deep charge-discharge cycles under 100 mA/gSb.  Also, because of the efficient 1-dimensional Na-ion transport pathway and the highly conductive network of SbNP@C, the electrode preserved high overall capacities even when cycled at high currents, extending its usability to high power applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrCf3y1wC4rXLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg7jGE00HlKAw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtVWht7nJ&amp;md5=382586ead9328ea5a3721bf05276e705</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2019.05.008"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shao, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Understanding and Improving the Initial Coulombic Efficiency of High-Capacity Anode Materials for Practical Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Energy Stor.                         cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tunable Redox Chemistry and Stability of Radical Intermediates in 2D Covalent Organic Frameworks for High Performance Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Gu, Shuai; Wu, Shaofei; Cao, Lujie; Li, Minchan; Qin, Ning; Zhu, Jian; Wang, Zhiqiang; Li, Yingzhi; Li, Zhiqiang; Chen, Jingjing; Lu, Zhouguang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">141</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">24</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">9623-9628</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Radicals are inevitable intermediates during the charging and discharging of org. redox electrodes.  The increase of the reactivity of the radical intermediates is desirable to maximize the capacity and enhance the rate capability but is detrimental to cycling stability.  Therefore, it is a great challenge to controllably balance the redox reactivity and stability of radical intermediates to optimize the electrochem. properties with a good combination of high specific capacity, excellent rate capability, and long-term cycle life.  Herein, we reported the redox and tunable stability of radical intermediates in covalent org. frameworks (COFs) considered as high capacity and stable anode for sodium-ion batteries.  The comprehensive characterizations combined with theor. simulation confirmed that the redox of C-O· and α-C radical intermediates play an important role in the sodiation/desodiation process.  Specifically, the stacking behavior could be feasibly tuned by the thickness of 2D COFs, essentially detg. the redox reactivity and stability of the α-C radical intermediates and their contributive capacity.  The modulation of reversible redox chem. and stabilization mechanism of radical intermediates in COFs offers a novel entry to design novel high performance org. electrode materials for energy storage and conversion.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpPzOcqEyNgVbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg7jGE00HlKAw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhtVektrnM&amp;md5=a21881c5d5f0abcf513bb0289ad60378</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref49'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit49" data-doi="10.1021/jp074464w"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Polleux, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lim, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dunn, B.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Pseudocapacitive Contributions to Electrochemical Energy Storage in TiO<sub>2</sub> (Anatase) Nanoparticles</span>. <i>J. Phys. Chem. C</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2007</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>111</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">40</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">14925</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">14931</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pseudocapacitive Contributions to Electrochemical Energy Storage in TiO2 (Anatase) Nanoparticles</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, John; Polleux, Julien; Lim, James; Dunn, Bruce</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry C</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2007</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">111</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">40</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">14925-14931</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPCCCK</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The advantages of using nanostructured materials for electrochem. energy storage have focused on the benefits assocd. with short path lengths.  However, another contribution, capacitive effects which become increasingly important at nanoscale dimensions, was studied.  Nanocryst. TiO2 (anatase) was studied over a dimensional regime where both capacitive and Li intercalation processes contribute to the total stored charge.  An anal. of the voltammetric sweep data was used to distinguish between the amt. of charge stored by these 2 processes.  At particle sizes &lt;10 nm, capacitive contributions became increasingly important, leading to greater amts. of total stored charge (gravimetrically normalized) with decreasing TiO2 particle size.  The area normalized capacitance is well &gt;100 μF/cm2, confirming that the capacitive contribution was pseudocapacitive.  Also, decreasing the particle size to the nanoscale regime led to faster charge/discharge rates because diffusion-controlled Li ion intercalation was replaced by faradaic reactions which occur at the surface of the material.  The charge storage and kinetic benefits derived from using nanoscale metal oxides provide an interesting direction for the design of materials that offer both power d. and energy d.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq0ueeFhvSDZLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljBZtP7O7NABw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD2sXhtVChs7zL&amp;md5=b47809cb86f6cf28f5758e0eb3eac71e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref50'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit50" data-doi="10.1038/s41578-019-0142-z"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Choi, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ashby, D.                         cas_cit51R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">51</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Covalent Coupling-Stabilized Transition-Metal Sulfide/Carbon Nanotube Composites for Lithium/Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hou, Tianyi; Liu, Borui; Sun, Xiaohong; Fan, Anran; Xu, Zhongkai; Cai, Shu; Zheng, Chunming; Yu, Guihua; Tricoli, Antonio</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">15</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6735-6746</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition-metal sulfides (TMSs) powered by conversion and/or alloying reactions are considered to be promising anode materials for advanced lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) and sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  However, the limited electronic cond. and large vol. expansion severely hinder their practical application.  Herein, we report a covalent coupling strategy for TMS-based anode materials using amide linkages to bind TMSs and carbon nanotubes (CNTs).  In the synthesis, the thiourea acts as not only the capping agent for morphol. control but also the linking agent for the covalent coupling.  As a proof of concept, the covalently coupled ZnS/CNT composite (CC-ZnS/CNT) has been prepd., with ZnS nanoparticles (~ 10 nm) tightly anchored on CNT bundles.  The compact ZnS-CNT heterojunctions are greatly beneficial to facilitating the electron/ion transfer and ensuring structural stability.  Due to the strong coupling interaction between ZnS and CNTs, the composite presents prominent pseudocapacitive behavior and highly reversible electrochem. processes, thus leading to superior long-term stability and excellent rate capability, delivering reversible capacities of 333 mAh g-1 at 2 A g-1 over 4000 cycles for LIBs and 314 mAh g-1 at 5 A g-1 after 500 cycles for SIBs.  Consequently, CC-ZnS/CNT exhibits great competence for applications in LIBs and SIBs, and the covalent coupling strategy is proposed as a promising approach for designing high-performance anode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpZBw1KdNa61bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljBZtP7O7NABw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXmvVCksr8%253D&amp;md5=dd6faf5db1e47beb94071541b2892f8e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref52"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref52'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">52</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit52" data-doi="10.1002/advs.201900028"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">MoS<sub>2</sub>-Coupled Carbon Nanosheets Encapsulated on Sodium Titanate Nanowires as Super-Durable Anode Material for Sodium-ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.     <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1900028</span>

    </div><div class="casAbstract">There is an ever-increasing demand for rechargeable batteries with fast charging, long cycling, high safety, and low cost in new energy storage systems.  Herein, a heterogeneous architecture composed of MoS2-coupled carbon nanosheets encapsulated on sodium titanate nanowires is developed and demonstrated as an advanced anode for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Owing to the synergistic effects of ultrastable substrate of 1D sodium titanate (NTO) nanowires, high-capacity promoter of 2D MoS2 nanosheets as well as the 2D conductive carbon matrix, the resulting 1D/2D-2D hybrid demonstrates excellent high-rate capacity and super-durable cyclability, delivering a stable capacity of up to 425.5 mAh g(-1) at 200 mA g(-1).  Even at an ultrafast charging/discharging process within 80 s, the capacity can be maintained at 201 mAh g(-1) after 16 000 cycles with only 0.0012% capacity loss per cycle, one of the best high-rate capacities and cyclabilities for NTO-based hybrid composites.  The present work highlights the designing protocol of hierarchical nanoarchitectures with stable substrate and high-capacity electrodes for next-generation energy storage applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcRlmp5_rt0De-vW160gIxP_fW6udTcc2eZj08DOm94w0rntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BB3M7pvF2msQ%253D%253D&amp;md5=ec72e8b4bc79cb980e3fa0ba96d22018</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref53"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref53'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">53</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit53" data-doi="10.1002/advs.201800763"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Men, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lin, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">CoSe<sub>2</sub> Nanoparticles Encapsulated by N-doped Carbon Framework Intertwined with Carbon Nanotubes: High-Performance Dual-Role Anode Materials for Both Li- and Na-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv. Sci.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>5</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">12</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">1800763</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit53R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">53</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">CoSe2 Nanoparticles Encapsulated by N-Doped Carbon Framework Intertwined with Carbon Nanotubes: High-Performance Dual-Role Anode Materials for Both Li- and Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang Jun; Gao Hongcheng; Men Shuang; Kang Xiongwu; Chen Shaowei; Shi Zhenqing; Lin Zhang; Chen Shaowei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced science (Weinheim, Baden-Wurttemberg, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1800763</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2198-3844</span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">It is of fundamental and technological significance to develop dual-role anode materials for both lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) and sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) with high performance.  Here, a composite material based on CoSe2 nanoparticles encapsulated in N-doped carbon framework intertwined with carbon nanotubes (CoSe2@N-CF/CNTs) is prepared successfully from cobalt-based zeolitic imidazolate framework (ZIF-67).  As anode materials for LIBs, CoSe2@N-CF/CNTs composites deliver a reversible capacity of 428 mAh g(-1) even after 500 cycles at a current density of 1 A g(-1) with almost 100% Coulombic efficiency.  The charge and discharge mechanisms of CoSe2 are characterized using ex situ X-ray diffraction and Raman analysis, from which the lithiation products of CoSe2 are found to be Li x CoSe2 and Li2Se, which are further converted to CoSe2 upon delithiation.  The CoSe2@N-CF/CNTs composites also demonstrate excellent electrochemical performance as anode materials for SIBs with a carbonate-based electrolyte, with specific capacities of 606 and 501 mAh g(-1) at 0.1 and 1 A g(-1) in the 100th cycle.  The electrochemical performance of the anode materials is further studied by pseudocapacitance and galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) measurements.  This work may be exploited for the rational design and development of dual-role anode materials for both Li- and Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcTca5WYW14WArHHuJhbyicZfW6udTcc2eZj08DOm94w0rntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BB3cnlt1aktA%253D%253D&amp;md5=83f84184ba5b0a849befd4a5b336ff1b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref54"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref54'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">54</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit54" data-doi="10.1007/s42765-022-00162-7"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zan, G.</span>; <span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, T.</span>; <span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, W.</span>; <span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, J.</span>; <span class="NLM_string-name">Tu, T.</span>; <span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, R.</span>; <span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Y.</span>; <span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span>; <span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Q.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Two-Level Biomimetic Designs Enable Intelligent Stress Dispersion for Super-Foldable C/NiS Nanofiber Free-Standing Electrode</span>.  <i>Adv. Eng. J.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>427</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">130936</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.cej.2021.130936</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D427%26publication_year%3D2022%26pages%3D130936%26journal%3DChem.%2BEng.%2BJ.%26author%3DY.%2BZhang%26author%3DJ.%2BLi%26author%3DL.%2BMa%26author%3DH.%2BLi%26author%3DX.%2BXu%26author%3DX.%2BLiu%26author%3DT.%2BLu%26author%3DL.%2BPan%26title%3DInsights%2Binto%2Bthe%2BStorage%2BMechanism%2Bof%2B3D%2BNanoflower-Like%2BV3S4%2BAnode%2Bin%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.cej.2021.130936&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.2c06551&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.cej.2021.130936&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit55R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">55</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Insights into the storage mechanism of 3D nanoflower-like V3S4 anode in sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Yajuan; Li, Jinliang; Ma, Liang; Li, Haibo; Xu, Xingtao; Liu, Xinjuan; Lu, Ting; Pan, Likun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">427</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">130936</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMEJAJ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1385-8947</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Over the past years, transition metal sulfides, with remarkable redox reversibility, favorable elec. cond. and superb theor. capacity, have received considerable attention on the development of electrode materials that are capable of efficient and reversible storage of sodium ions.  In this work, three-dimensional (3D) nanoflower-like V3S4 was applied into sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) as anode, which was successfully synthesized via a facile solvothermal process with post-calcination treatment.  The electrochem. measurements demonstrate that the as-prepd. V3S4 delivers a high reversible capacity of 499 mAh g-1 after 100 cycles at 0.1 A g-1.  Furthermore, even at a high c.d. of 5 A g-1, the V3S4 also exhibits an outstanding specific capacity of 299 mAh g-1 and a capacity retention rate of 58% compared with the capacity at 0.1 A g-1, which are superior to those of most vanadium sulfides for SIBs reported previously.  Remarkably, the ultrahigh sodium-ion storage performance of V3S4 should be ascribed to the unique nanoflower-like structure assembled by ultrathin nanosheets, which not only provides a large sp. surface area, but also offers an adequate cushion to suppress the vol. expansion during the sodiation-desodiation processes.  More importantly, operando Raman spectra, ex-situ X-ray diffraction and ex-situ XPS were employed to demonstrate the evolution of the structure and chem. valence of V3S4, revealing that the high capacity of V3S4 results from the cooperation of Na+ intercalation and conversion reaction.  The findings of this study provide a better understanding on the sodium storage mechanism of V3S4.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoseqVtdgVzMrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljBZtP7O7NABw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhsVagtrjK&amp;md5=f7a9ad6752588f4c0e48a01d79b210a6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref56"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref56'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">56</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit56" data-doi="10.1021/acssuschemeng.9b07714"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lin, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Synthesis of ZIF-Derived CoS<sub>2</sub> Nanocages Interconnected by CNTs for Rechargeable Li–O<sub>2</sub> Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Sustain.
